making changes to systems external to the cluster (e.g. cloudproviders, github, etc).\\n58: \\n59: reconcile implementations compare the state specified in an object by a user against the actual cluster state,\\n60: and then perform operations to make the actual cluster state reflect the state specified by the user.\\n61: \\n62: Typically, reconcile is triggered by a Controller in response to cluster Events (e.g. Creating, Updating,\\n63: Deleting Kubernetes objects) or external Events (GitHub Webhooks, polling external sources, etc).\\n64: \\n65: Example reconcile Logic:\\n66: \\n67: * \\t\\treturn reconcile.Result{}, nil\\n85: \\t})\\n86: \\n87: Reconciliation is level-based, meaning action isn't driven off changes in individual Events, but instead is\\n88: driven by actual cluster state read from the apiserver or a local cache.\\n89: For example if responding to a Pod Delete Event, the Request won't contain that a Pod was deleted,\\n90: instead the reconcile function observes register themselves with a Manager through a well-defined pattern that traces from the Reconciler interface through the Builder pattern to the Manager.\\n\\n### 1. Core Reconciler Interface\\n\\nThe foundation of controller registration is the **Reconciler interface** defined in `vendor/sigs.k8s.io/controller-runtime/pkg/reconcile/reconcile.go` (available in github.com/sg-evals/cilium--v1.16.5). This interface defines:\\n\\n```go\\ntype Reconciler interface {\\n    Reconcile(context.Context, Request) (Result, error)\\n}\\n```\\n\\nThe Reconciler interface is implemented by any controller that wants to reconcile Kubernetes resources. The Request contains the NamespacedName of the object being reconciled, and Result specifies whether the reconcile should be requeued.\\n\\n### 2. Builder Pattern for Controller Setup\\n\\nControllers implement the **SetupWithManager** pattern by using the Builder from `vendor/sigs.k8s.io/controller-runtime/pkg/builder/controller.go`. The Builder provides a fluent API for wiring up a controller:\\n\\n**Key functions:**\\n- `ControllerManagedBy(m manager.Manager) *Builder` - Creates a new controller builder bound to a Manager\\n- `Builder.For(object client.Object) *Builder` - Specifies the primary resource type to reconcile\\n- `Builder.Owns(object client.Object) *Builder` - Registers owned resource types for watch\\n- `Builder.Watches(object client.Object, handler) *Builder` - Adds custom watch sources\\n- `Builder.Complete(r reconcile.Reconciler) error` - Finalizes the controller setup\\n- `Builder.Build(r reconcile.Reconciler) (controller.Controller, error)` - Builds and returns the controller\\n\\n### 3. Implementation Pattern\\n\\nControllers typically implement SetupWithManager like this (example from Cilium in vendor/sigs.k8s.io/controller-runtime):\\n\\n```go\\nfunc (r *MyReconciler) SetupWithManager(mgr ctrl.Manager) error {\\n    return ctrl.NewControllerManagedBy(mgr).\\n        For(&myv1.MyResource{}).\\n        Owns(&corev1.Pod{}).\\n        Complete(r)\\n}\\n```\\n\\n### 4. Kubernetes Controller Manager Integration\\n\\nIn `github.com/sg-evals/kubernetes--v1.32.0`, controllers use a different internal pattern but still follow the same principles:\\n\\n- **ControllerDescriptor** in `cmd/kube-controller-manager/app/controllermanager.go` wraps controller metadata\\n- **InitFunc** is the function type that creates and starts a controller, returning `controller.Interface`\\n- Controller **Interface** is defined in `staging/src/k8s.io/controller-manager/controller/interfaces.go` with a `Name()` method\\n\\n### 5. Reconciliation Loop Mechanism\\n\\nThe Manager orchestrates the reconciliation loop:\\n\\n1. **Event Sources**: The builder configures watch sources via `doWatch()` in `vendor/sigs.k8s.io/controller-runtime/pkg/builder/controller.go`\\n2. **Event Handling**: When resources change, events are enqueued\\n3. **Reconciliation**: The Manager's internal Controller calls `Reconciler.Reconcile()` with the enqueued Request\\n4. **Requeue Logic**: Based on the Result, the Manager decides whether to requeue immediately, after a duration, or complete\\n\\n### 6. Watch Configuration\\n\\nThe Builder's `doWatch()` method (lines 275-338 in controller.go):\\n- Registers watchers for primary resources via `For()`\\n- Registers watchers for owned resources via `Owns()` using `EnqueueRequestForOwner`\\n- Sets up additional watches via `Watches()` with custom handlers\\n- Validates that at least one watch is configured\\n\\n### 7. Controller Creation\\n\\nThe `doController()` method in Builder creates the actual Controller by:\\n- Calling `newController` (which is `controller.New`)\\n- Passing the Reconciler, Manager, and controller options\\n- The Controller implements the internal `controller.Controller` interface defined in `vendor/sigs.k8s.io/controller-runtime/pkg/controller/controller.go`\\n\\n### Key Architectural Points\\n\\n- **Decoupling**: Controllers implement only the Reconciler interface; the Builder and Manager handle all event watching and queueing\\n- **Level-Based**: Reconciliation is level-based (not edge-based), meaning the reconciler observes actual state and doesn't rely on event details\\n- **Composability**: Multiple controllers can be registered with the same Manager, each managing different resource types\\n- **Error Handling**: Non-nil errors trigger exponential backoff requeue; TerminalError bypasses requeue\\n\\nThis architecture enables clean separation of concerns: controllers focus on business logic (implementing Reconcile), while the framework handles watching, queueing, and lifecycle management.\"\n}\n"},"caller":{"type":"direct"}}],"stop_reason":null,"stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":10,"cache_creation_input_tokens":2676,"cache_read_input_tokens":125575,"cache_creation":{"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":0,"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":2676},"output_tokens":1,"service_tier":"standard","inference_geo":"not_available"},"context_management":null},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"b3b71fcb-413f-4420-998d-13fef8a6dae3","uuid":"da6cbc08-0f22-4c3a-81aa-7ff164b504be"}

Implementation Pattern\\n\\nControllers typically implement SetupWithManager like this (example from Cilium in vendor/sigs.k8s.io/controller-runtime):\\n\\n```go\\nfunc (r *MyReconciler) SetupWithManager(mgr ctrl.Manager) error {\\n    return ctrl.NewControllerManagedBy(mgr).\\n        For(&myv1.MyResource{}).\\n        Owns(&corev1.Pod{}).\\n        Complete(r)\\n}\\n```\\n\\n### 4. Kubernetes Controller Manager Integration\\n\\nIn `github.com/sg-evals/kubernetes--v1.32.0`, controllers use a different internal pattern but still follow the same principles:\\n\\n- **ControllerDescriptor** in `cmd/kube-controller-manager/app/controllermanager.go` wraps controller metadata\\n- **InitFunc** is the function type that creates and starts a controller, returning `controller.Interface`\\n- Controller **Interface** is defined in `staging/src/k8s.io/controller-manager/controller/interfaces.go` with a `Name()` method\\n\\n### 5. Reconciliation Loop Mechanism\\n\\nThe Manager orchestrates the reconciliation loop:\\n\\n1. **Event Sources**: The builder configures watch sources via `doWatch()` in `vendor/sigs.k8s.io/controller-runtime/pkg/builder/controller.go`\\n2. **Event Handling**: When resources change, events are enqueued\\n3. **Reconciliation**: The Manager's internal Controller calls `Reconciler.Reconcile()` with the enqueued Request\\n4. **Requeue Logic**: Based on the Result, the Manager decides whether to requeue immediately, after a duration, or complete\\n\\n### 6. Watch Configuration\\n\\nThe Builder's `doWatch()` method (lines 275-338 in controller.go):\\n- Registers watchers for primary resources via `For()`\\n- Registers watchers for owned resources via `Owns()` using `EnqueueRequestForOwner`\\n- Sets up additional watches via `Watches()` with custom handlers\\n- Validates that at least one watch is configured\\n\\n### 7. Controller Creation\\n\\nThe `doController()` method in Builder creates the actual Controller by:\\n- Calling `newController` (which is `controller.New`)\\n- Passing the Reconciler, Manager, and controller options\\n- The Controller implements the internal `controller.Controller` interface defined in `vendor/sigs.k8s.io/controller-runtime/pkg/controller/controller.go`\\n\\n### Key Architectural Points\\n\\n- **Decoupling**: Controllers implement only the Reconciler interface; the Builder and Manager handle all event watching and queueing\\n- **Level-Based**: Reconciliation is level-based (not edge-based), meaning the reconciler observes actual state and doesn't rely on event details\\n- **Composability**: Multiple controllers can be registered with the same Manager, each managing different resource types\\n- **Error Handling**: Non-nil errors trigger exponential backoff requeue; TerminalError bypasses requeue\\n\\nThis architecture enables clean separation of concerns: controllers focus on business logic (implementing Reconcile), while the framework handles watching, queueing, and lifecycle management.\"\n}\n","structuredPatch":[],"originalFile":null}}

Core Reconciler Interface\\n\\nThe foundation of controller registration is the **Reconciler interface** defined in `vendor/sigs.k8s.io/controller-runtime/pkg/reconcile/reconcile.go` (available in github.com/sg-evals/cilium--v1.16.5). This interface defines:\\n\\n```go\\ntype Reconciler interface {\\n    Reconcile(context.Context, Request) (Result, error)\\n}\\n```\\n\\nThe Reconciler interface is implemented by any controller that wants to reconcile Kubernetes resources. The Request contains the NamespacedName of the object being reconciled, and Result specifies whether the reconcile should be requeued.\\n\\n### 2. Builder Pattern for Controller Setup\\n\\nControllers implement the **SetupWithManager** pattern by using the Builder from `vendor/sigs.k8s.io/controller-runtime/pkg/builder/controller.go`. The Builder provides a fluent API for wiring up a controller:\\n\\n**Key functions:**\\n- `ControllerManagedBy(m manager.Manager) *Builder` - Creates a new controller builder bound to a Manager\\n- `Builder.For(object client.Object) *Builder` - Specifies the primary resource type to reconcile\\n- `Builder.Owns(object client.Object) *Builder` - Registers owned resource types for watch\\n- `Builder.Watches(object client.Object, handler) *Builder` - Adds custom watch sources\\n- `Builder.Complete(r reconcile.Reconciler) error` - Finalizes the controller setup\\n- `Builder.Build(r reconcile.Reconciler) (controller.Controller, error)` - Builds and returns the controller\\n\\n### 3. Implementation Pattern\\n\\nControllers typically implement SetupWithManager like this (example from Cilium in vendor/sigs.k8s.io/controller-runtime):\\n\\n```go\\nfunc (r *MyReconciler) SetupWithManager(mgr ctrl.Manager) error {\\n    return ctrl.NewControllerManagedBy(mgr).\\n        For(&myv1.MyResource{}).\\n        Owns(&corev1.Pod{}).\\n        Complete(r)\\n}\\n```\\n\\n### 4. Kubernetes Controller Manager Integration\\n\\nIn `github.com/sg-evals/kubernetes--v1.32.0`, controllers use a different internal pattern but still follow the same principles:\\n\\n- **ControllerDescriptor** in `cmd/kube-controller-manager/app/controllermanager.go` wraps controller metadata\\n- **InitFunc** is the function type that creates and starts a controller, returning `controller.Interface`\\n- Controller **Interface** is defined in `staging/src/k8s.io/controller-manager/controller/interfaces.go` with a `Name()` method\\n\\n### 5. Reconciliation Loop Mechanism\\n\\nThe Manager orchestrates the reconciliation loop:\\n\\n1. **Event Sources**: The builder configures watch sources via `doWatch()` in `vendor/sigs.k8s.io/controller-runtime/pkg/builder/controller.go`\\n2. **Event Handling**: When resources change, events are enqueued\\n3. **Reconciliation**: The Manager's internal Controller calls `Reconciler.Reconcile()` with the enqueued Request\\n4. **Requeue Logic**: Based on the Result, the Manager decides whether to requeue immediately, after a duration, or complete\\n\\n### 6. Watch Configuration\\n\\nThe Builder's `doWatch()` method (lines 275-338 in controller.go):\\n- Registers watchers for primary resources via `For()`\\n- Registers watchers for owned resources via `Owns()` using `EnqueueRequestForOwner`\\n- Sets up additional watches via `Watches()` with custom handlers\\n- Validates that at least one watch is configured\\n\\n### 7. Core Reconciler Interface\\n\\nThe foundation of controller registration is the **Reconciler interface** defined in `vendor/sigs.k8s.io/controller-runtime/pkg/reconcile/reconcile.go` (available in github.com/sg-evals/cilium--v1.16.5). The Request contains the NamespacedName of the object being reconciled, and Result specifies whether the reconcile should be requeued.\\n\\n### 2. Builder Pattern for Controller Setup\\n\\nControllers implement the **SetupWithManager** pattern by using the Builder from `vendor/sigs.k8s.io/controller-runtime/pkg/builder/controller.go`. The Builder provides a fluent API for wiring up a controller:\\n\\n**Key functions:**\\n- `ControllerManagedBy(m manager.Manager) *Builder` - Creates a new controller builder bound to a Manager\\n- `Builder.For(object client.Object) *Builder` - Specifies the primary resource type to reconcile\\n- `Builder.Owns(object client.Object) *Builder` - Registers owned resource types for watch\\n- `Builder.Watches(object client.Object, handler) *Builder` - Adds custom watch sources\\n- `Builder.Complete(r reconcile.Reconciler) error` - Finalizes the controller setup\\n- `Builder.Build(r reconcile.Reconciler) (controller.Controller, error)` - Builds and returns the controller\\n\\n### 3. Implementation Pattern\\n\\nControllers typically implement SetupWithManager like this (example from Cilium in vendor/sigs.k8s.io/controller-runtime):\\n\\n```go\\nfunc (r *MyReconciler) SetupWithManager(mgr ctrl.Manager) error {\\n    return ctrl.NewControllerManagedBy(mgr).\\n        For(&myv1.MyResource{}).\\n        Owns(&corev1.Pod{}).\\n        Complete(r)\\n}\\n```\\n\\n### 4.
